## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate expressed as a function of time t and population size P, which is the standard setup for ecological/demographic growth models written as differential equations. Common structures encode density-independent growth (proportional to P), density dependence (crowding/carrying capacity), thresholds (Allee effects), and time-varying vital rates (seasonality or trends).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, per-capita rate constant)
- Linear growth/decay ODE: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (net immigration/emigration plus proportional growth/decline)
- Power-law (allometric) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (phenomenological scaling of growth with size)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding causes growth-rate curvature; c1<0 gives self-limitation)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic crowding; often fits microbial/tumor growth)
- Theta-logistic (generalized crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (tunable strength of density dependence)
- Richards/generalized logistic rate form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (flexible sigmoidal approach; varying inflection shape)
- Allee effect with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (low-density suppression plus high-density limitation)
- Constant-yield harvesting/stocking: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 (c2<0 harvest; c2>0 stocking/immigration)
- Proportional harvesting (fishing mortality): dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (extra linear loss term)
- Seasonally forced per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting births/deaths)
- Trend in per-capita rate (environmental change): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * P (time-varying growth/decline independent of density)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P over a range, expect density-independent (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt ~ c * P.
- If dP_dt becomes negative at large P and is well-fit by a concave parabola vs P, quadratic self-limitation is indicated: dP_dt ~ c1 * P + c2 * P**2 with c2<0.
- If per-capita growth (dP_dt / P) decreases roughly linearly with log(P), a Gompertz structure is suggested: dP_dt ~ P * log(K/P).
- If the approach to a ceiling depends strongly on an extra shape parameter (earlier/later inflection), use generalized crowding exponents: (1 - (c*P)**theta) or its powered variants.
- If growth is suppressed at low P but positive at intermediate P, include an Allee factor producing a threshold/root at small P: P*(c*P-1).
- If dP_dt has nonzero value near P≈0 (positive or negative), include additive immigration/harvest terms: +c0.
- If oscillations in dP_dt persist at similar relative amplitude when scaled by P, model forcing in the per-capita rate: (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t+c3))*P.
- If dP_dt/P drifts over time even at similar P, encode explicit time dependence in coefficients (e.g., exponential trend in t multiplying P).
